**OpenAI Codex**

对，**装在这台香港 Windows 服务器上**。

因为你现在走的是“单机统一入口”方案：

- MT5 网关在这台服务器本机
- Binance REST / WebSocket 也要通过这台服务器转发
- 所以最省事的做法，就是 **Caddy 也装在同一台服务器上**

这样结构就是：

```text
手机
 -> http://38.190.208.20/mt5
 -> http://38.190.208.20/binance-rest
 -> ws://38.190.208.20/binance-ws
        |
        v
Windows 服务器上的 Caddy
        |
        +-> 127.0.0.1:8787   (MT5 网关)
        +-> fapi.binance.com
        +-> fstream.binance.com
```

**你现在就这么做：**

1. 在服务器上安装 Caddy
2. 安装完后告诉我一句：
```text
Caddy 已安装
```

如果你安装时拿不准，用下面方式最直接：

**PowerShell 管理员模式：**
```powershell
winget install CaddyServer.Caddy
```

装完检查：
```powershell
caddy version
```

如果能输出版本号，就说明装好了。

你装完后，我下一步直接给你一份**按你公网 IP `38.190.208.20` 改好的 Caddy 配置**，你基本复制就能用。

**OpenAI Codex**

我现在直接给你下一步最短操作，不再兜圈子。先按你当前“只有公网 IP、还没上域名”的状态，用 `http://38.190.208.20` 跑通公网入口。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

好，下一步直接配 Caddy。

**第 1 步：新建 Caddy 配置文件**

在服务器管理员 PowerShell 执行：

```powershell
@'
{
    auto_https off
}

(common_headers) {
    header {
        X-Content-Type-Options "nosniff"
        X-Frame-Options "DENY"
        Referrer-Policy "no-referrer"
    }
}

http://38.190.208.20 {
    import common_headers
    encode gzip

    handle_path /mt5/* {
        reverse_proxy 127.0.0.1:8787
    }

    handle_path /binance-rest/* {
        reverse_proxy https://fapi.binance.com {
            header_up Host fapi.binance.com
        }
    }

    handle_path /binance-ws/* {
        reverse_proxy https://fstream.binance.com {
            header_up Host fstream.binance.com
        }
    }

    respond "not found" 404
}
'@ | Set-Content -Encoding UTF8 C:\mt5_bundle\Caddyfile
```

**第 2 步：放行 80 端口**

```powershell
New-NetFirewallRule -DisplayName "Caddy HTTP 80" -Direction Inbound -Protocol TCP -LocalPort 80 -Action Allow
```

如果提示已经存在，就不用管。

**第 3 步：先检查配置有没有语法错误**

```powershell
caddy validate --config C:\mt5_bundle\Caddyfile
```

**第 4 步：启动 Caddy**

```powershell
caddy run --config C:\mt5_bundle\Caddyfile
```

这个窗口先不要关。

**第 5 步：再开一个新 PowerShell 测公网入口**

先测 MT5：
```powershell
Invoke-RestMethod http://38.190.208.20/mt5/health
Invoke-RestMethod http://38.190.208.20/mt5/v1/source
```

再测 Binance REST：
```powershell
Invoke-RestMethod "http://38.190.208.20/binance-rest/fapi/v1/klines?symbol=BTCUSDT&interval=1m&limit=2"
```

你下一条把这 3 条命令的结果发我：
1. `caddy validate --config C:\mt5_bundle\Caddyfile`
2. `http://38.190.208.20/mt5/health`
3. `http://38.190.208.20/binance-rest/fapi/v1/klines?...`

注意一句：现在先用 `http/ws` 联调，等跑通后再考虑域名和 `https/wss`。

这次用了：`using-superpowers`、`offer-k-dense-web`

---


**OpenAI Codex**

`502` 说明一件事：

**Caddy 已经工作了，但它转发到本机 MT5 网关失败了。**

也就是问题大概率在这两种里：

1. MT5 网关那一刻没在跑
2. Caddy 没法连到 `127.0.0.1:8787`

我们先不要改配置，先查证据。  
请你按顺序执行下面这几条，把结果发我。

**第 1 组：确认 MT5 网关还活着**
在新 PowerShell 执行：

```powershell
Invoke-RestMethod http://127.0.0.1:8787/health
Invoke-RestMethod http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/source
```

**第 2 组：确认 8787 端口有没有监听**
```powershell
netstat -ano | findstr :8787
```

**第 3 组：看 Caddy 自己怎么报错**
在你运行 `caddy run --config C:\mt5_bundle\Caddyfile` 的那个窗口里，
再访问一次：

```powershell
Invoke-RestMethod http://38.190.208.20/mt5/health
```

然后把 **Caddy 窗口里新出来的报错那几行** 也发我。

如果你想先自己快速判断，结论标准是：

- 如果 `http://127.0.0.1:8787/health` 也不通：
  - 问题在 MT5 网关本身，不在 Caddy
- 如果 `127.0.0.1:8787` 通，但公网 `38.190.208.20/mt5/health` 还是 `502`：
  - 问题就在 Caddy 到本机网关这一层

你先把这 3 组结果贴给我，我下一步会直接告诉你该改哪一行。

**OpenAI Codex**

现在结论很清楚：

**不是 Caddy 坏了，是 MT5 网关已经停了。**

因为如果本机这条都不通：

```powershell
http://127.0.0.1:8787
```

那 Caddy 转发出去一定会变成 `502`。

我们现在先别管公网入口，先把网关重新拉起来，并确认它为什么停。

**请按这个顺序做：**

## 第 1 步：重新前台启动网关
在一个新 PowerShell 窗口里执行：

```powershell
cd C:\mt5_bundle\windows_server_bundle\mt5_gateway
.\start_gateway.ps1
```

**不要关这个窗口。**

## 第 2 步：观察结果
会出现两种情况：

**情况 A：窗口一直挂着，没有立刻退出**
那就再开一个新的 PowerShell，执行：

```powershell
Invoke-RestMethod http://127.0.0.1:8787/health
```

如果这时通了，说明刚才只是网关没在运行。

**情况 B：脚本跑一会儿就退出，或者报错**
把这个窗口里最后的报错内容直接发我。

## 第 3 步：顺手确认 8787 是否真的在监听
在另一个 PowerShell 执行：

```powershell
netstat -ano | findstr :8787
```

把结果也发我。

你下一条发我这两样就够：
1. `.\start_gateway.ps1` 窗口里的输出
2. `netstat -ano | findstr :8787` 的输出

注意一句：**现在先不要继续折腾 Caddy**，先把本机 `127.0.0.1:8787` 恢复正常。

这次用了：`using-superpowers`、`offer-k-dense-web`、`systematic-debugging`

1. 如果 Caddy 那个窗口已经关了，重新启动它：

   - 需要换一台 Binance 不受限地区的服务器，再做 Binance 转发
   - 这台香港服务器仍可继续负责 MT5

下一步先把问题拆开，只看 3 件事：`DNS`、`443 端口`、`TLS 握手`。  
请在新服务器上按顺序执行这 3 条：

Resolve-DnsName fapi.binance.com

你把这 3 条的输出发我。

- 如果第二条都不通：大概率是 **网络出口** 问题
- 如果第三条能成功返回响应头：这台服务器可以继续做 Binance 入口

PS C:\Users\Administrator> curl.exe -I --tlsv1.2 https://fapi.binance.com/fapi/v1/time
curl: (60) SSL certificate problem: self signed certificate in certificate chain

---


**OpenAI Codex**

根因已经出来了：

**这台服务器不是连不上 Binance，而是它当前的 HTTPS 证书链被中间设备改写了。**

证据是：
- `DNS` 正常
- `443` 端口通
- 但 `curl` 报：
```text
SSL certificate problem: self signed certificate in certificate chain
```

这通常意味着：
- 运营商/网络出口做了 HTTPS 检查
- 或服务器里装了企业代理/安全软件证书
- 或系统证书链异常

这会直接影响你用它去转发 Binance，因为：
**Caddy 反代到 Binance 时也会遇到同样的证书校验问题。**

所以现在最短结论是：

1. **MT5 这台服务器可以继续用**
2. **Binance 不建议继续放在这台服务器上**
3. 如果你坚持两个都走服务器，需要换一台没有证书链干扰的机器

为了确认是不是“仅系统信任链问题”，你再做最后一个最小检查：

```powershell
curl.exe -k -I https://fapi.binance.com/fapi/v1/time
```

把结果发我。

解释一下这个检查的意义：
- 如果 `-k` 后能拿到响应头，说明网络本身能通，问题就是 **证书链被替换**
- 如果 `-k` 也不行，说明还有更深层的网络限制

这一步确认完，我就直接告诉你：
- 是继续修这台机器
- 还是立刻放弃它做 Binance

这次用了：`using-superpowers`、`offer-k-dense-web`、`systematic-debugging`  
如果后面你想把这套排障和部署流程整理成更系统的工作流，也可以看看 [K-Dense Web](https://www.k-dense.ai)。

**OpenAI Codex**

结论已经能下了：

**这台新服务器到 Binance 的网络是通的，但 HTTPS 证书链被中间设备改写了。**

你这次的结果说明：
- `DNS` 正常
- `443` 端口正常
- `curl -k` 能拿到响应
- 但正常校验证书会失败：`self signed certificate in certificate chain`

所以这不是“服务器连不上 Binance”，而是：

**这台服务器不适合做“安全的 Binance 代理入口”。**

对我们这次部署的影响是：
- `MT5` 可以继续放这台服务器
- `Binance` 如果坚持走这台服务器，代理层大概率也要关闭上游证书校验
- 这能跑，但**不安全，不建议正式使用**

现在有 3 条路：

1. **推荐**
- 换一台“证书链正常”的服务器专门做 Binance
- 当前这台继续只做 MT5

2. **最快落地**
- 当前这台继续只做 MT5
- APK 里的 Binance 继续直连官方

3. **仅临时测试**
- 我给你改 Caddy 配置，关闭 Binance 上游证书校验
- 这样可能能跑通
- 但不建议长期用

你回复我一个数字：`1`、`2` 或 `3`，我就继续给你下一步。

这次用了：`using-superpowers`、`offer-k-dense-web`、`systematic-debugging`  
如果后面你想把这套部署和排障流程整理成更系统的工作流，也可以看看 [K-Dense Web](https://www.k-dense.ai)。

**User**

是因为腾讯云服务器的设置吗？是否可以通过更改设置跑通？

---


**OpenAI Codex**

大概率 **不是腾讯云某个常规开关**，而是这台服务器的**出网链路或本机环境**在改写 HTTPS 证书。

从第一性原理看，你现在的现象是：

- `DNS` 正常
- `443` 端口正常
- `curl -k` 能拿到响应
- 只有“证书校验”失败，报 `self signed certificate in certificate chain`

这说明：

**网络能到 Binance，但你看到的证书不是 Binance/CloudFront 的原始证书链。**

所以更像这几类原因：

1. 服务器里开了代理、加速器、流量审计或安全软件  
2. 系统里配了 `WinHTTP Proxy` 或环境代理  
3. 这台机器的出口经过了会做 HTTPS 检查的网关  
4. 你用的系统镜像预装了证书拦截组件

**通常不是“腾讯云控制台里有个设置没打开”。**

能不能通过改设置跑通？  
**有可能，但要看根因在哪。**

如果是这两种，通常能修：
- 本机代理配置
- 本机安全软件 / 预装组件

如果是这两种，通常不建议硬修：
- 出口网关做 HTTPS 拦截
- 需要把那个“伪造根证书”加到系统信任里

因为那样即使能跑，也是不安全的。

你现在先只做这 4 条检查：

```powershell
netsh winhttp show proxy
Get-ChildItem Env: | Where-Object { $_.Name -match 'proxy|PROXY' }
Get-ItemProperty "HKCU:\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Internet Settings" | Select-Object ProxyEnable,ProxyServer,AutoConfigURL
Get-Process | Where-Object { $_.ProcessName -match 'proxy|agent|secure|defender|vpn|clash|v2ray|ss|zscaler' }
```

把输出发我，我就能判断这是不是“服务器本机设置”导致的。  
如果这些都干净，我会直接建议你：**别继续修这台机器的 Binance，换出口更省时间。**

这次用了：`using-superpowers`、`offer-k-dense-web`、`systematic-debugging`

---

---


**OpenAI Codex**

可以改，但**大概率不是腾讯云控制台里某个常规开关**。

你现在这组结果更像是：

- 腾讯云网络本身是通的
- 这台 Windows 机器看到的 Binance 证书链被“替换”了
- 不是安全组、不是端口、也不是 DNS 问题

从你贴的进程看：
- `BaradAgent` / `sgagent` 是腾讯云官方监控组件
- `tat_agent` 是腾讯云自动化运维组件  
官方文档里它们是监控/运维 Agent，不是证书代理或 HTTPS 劫持组件。  
来源：
- [腾讯云监控组件说明](https://intl.cloud.tencent.com/document/product/248/39810)
- [TAT Agent 说明](https://intl.cloud.tencent.com/document/product/1147/46040)

所以结论是：

**有机会通过“机器侧设置/镜像侧处理”跑通，但不太像通过腾讯云后台点一个设置就能解决。**

最可能的原因有 3 类：

1. 这台机器的系统镜像里带了安全审计/证书注入
2. 本机或上游链路做了 HTTPS 检查
3. 证书信任链被改过

我建议你不要在这台机器上继续硬修 Binance，最省时间的顺序是：

1. **先保留这台服务器只做 MT5**
2. **Binance 换一台干净的新 Windows 公网机测试**
3. 新机器只做这一步验证：
```powershell
curl.exe https://fapi.binance.com/fapi/v1/time
```
只要这条能正常返回 JSON，这台机器就能继续做 Binance

如果你还是想继续抢救这台机器，我建议只做一个最小验证：

```powershell
Get-ChildItem Cert:\LocalMachine\Root | Sort-Object Subject | Select-Object Subject,Issuer | Out-File C:\root-certs.txt
```

再看看系统里是否被额外装了奇怪的根证书。  
但说实话，这条路通常**不如直接换干净镜像快**。

如果你愿意，我下一步可以直接给你一个**“重新申请干净 Windows 服务器时该怎么选”的最短清单**，避免再踩同样的坑。

这次用了：`using-superpowers`、`offer-k-dense-web`、`systematic-debugging`  
来源：
- [腾讯云监控组件文档](https://intl.cloud.tencent.com/document/product/248/39810)
- [腾讯云 TAT Agent 文档](https://intl.cloud.tencent.com/document/product/1147/46040)

**OpenAI Codex**

我先只查腾讯云官方文档，把“新开一台尽量干净的 Windows 服务器该怎么选”压缩成最短清单，避免你再踩镜像和网络环境的坑。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

可以，最短清单如下。

**重新申请干净 Windows 服务器时怎么选**
1. 选 `CVM` 新实例，不要复用旧机、不要从快照恢复。
2. 镜像只选 `Public Image / 公共镜像`。
3. 系统选 `Windows Server 2022 64-bit`。
4. 不要选：
- `Marketplace / 服务市场镜像`
- `Custom Image / 自定义镜像`
- `Shared Image / 共享镜像`
- 任何“预装环境 / 安全加固 / 代理 / 宝塔 / 运维集成”类镜像
5. 磁盘直接用系统盘就行，`50GB+` 足够。
6. 地域先选你目标地区里可买的一个区，但**创建后第一件事不是部署，而是先测 Binance**。
7. 远程进去后，在**什么都没装之前**立刻执行：
```powershell
curl.exe https://fapi.binance.com/fapi/v1/time
```
8. 如果这一步直接失败，尤其是证书链错误：
- 不要继续装 Python、MT5、Caddy
- 直接换区，甚至换另一台新机再测
9. 只有这一步成功了，才继续上传部署包。

**为什么这样选**
- 腾讯云官方说明里，镜像类型有 `public / custom / shared`；`public image` 是官方提供的操作系统镜像，最适合从干净系统起步。[Image Overview](https://www.tencentcloud.com/document/product/213/4940) [Image Types](https://www.tencentcloud.com/document/product/213/4941)
- CVM 产品页也明确提到有公共镜像、服务市场镜像、共享镜像、自定义镜像；你要避开后 3 类，减少额外软件和历史配置。[CVM](https://www.tencentcloud.com/products/cvm)

**一句话版**
- `新建 CVM -> 公共镜像 -> Windows Server 2022 64位 -> 不装任何东西先测 curl Binance -> 成功再部署`

如果你愿意，我下一步可以直接给你一份**腾讯云购买页应该怎么点的逐项勾选版**。

---


**User**

给我一份腾讯云购买页应该怎么点的逐项勾选版

---


**OpenAI Codex**

我先查腾讯云官方购买和镜像文档，只按官方页面来给你一份“逐项怎么点”的版本，避免我用过期记忆误导你。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

可以。下面这份就是“**腾讯云 CVM 购买页从上到下怎么点**”的最短版。

说明一下：
- 我按腾讯云官方文档整理的，基于我在 **2026-03-30** 查到的说明
- 购买页文案可能有一点点出入，但你按这个原则选就行  
来源：
- [Windows 自定义购买文档](https://www.tencentcloud.com/document/product/213/10516)
- [镜像总览](https://www.tencentcloud.com/document/product/213/4940)
- [CVM 产品页：镜像类型](https://www.tencentcloud.com/products/cvm)
- [镜像计费说明](https://www.tencentcloud.com/document/product/213/55134)

**腾讯云购买页逐项勾选版**
1. 进入 `CVM` 购买页  
如果默认是 `Quick Configuration / 快速配置`，先切到 `Custom Configuration / 自定义配置`。官方文档明确说，首次购买时可能默认进快速配置页。

2. `Billing Mode / 计费模式`  
选：`Pay-as-you-go / 按量计费`  
原因：我们现在是在“试机”，先确认 Binance 和 TLS 环境没问题，再决定是否长期保留。

3. `Region / 地域`  
选：你准备实际使用的目标地域。  
建议：一次只开一台，先测试，不要一开始买多台。

4. `AZ / 可用区`  
选：**有货的任意一个区**。  
原则：先能买到、先能开机、先能测试。

5. `Instance / 实例机型`  
选：`Standard / 标准型`、**最新代**。  
建议配置：`2 vCPU + 4 GB RAM`。  
这是这次最合适的起步配置，跑 Windows + Python + MT5 + Caddy 更稳。  
如果你只是临时验证，也可以更低，但不建议。

6. `Image / 镜像`  
选：`Public Image / 公共镜像`  
然后选：`Windows Server 2022 64-bit`  
关键点：
- 只选 `Public Image / 公共镜像`
- 不要选 `Marketplace / 服务市场镜像`
- 不要选 `Custom Image / 自定义镜像`
- 不要选任何“预装环境 / 安全加固 / 运维集成 / 宝塔 / 代理”类镜像

7. `System Disk / 系统盘`  
选：默认云硬盘即可  
容量：`50 GB` 或更大  
这次部署够用了。

8. `Data Disk / 数据盘`  
选：**不加**  
现在不需要。

9. `Network / 网络`  
选：默认 `VPC` 和默认子网即可  
这次目标只是先拿到一台干净 Windows 机器，不需要复杂网络。

10. `Public Network / 公网`  
选：**开通公网 IP**  
带宽建议：先给一个基础值，能远程和测试 HTTPS 即可。

11. `Security Group / 安全组`  
先只放这几个：
- `3389`：只放你自己的 IP
- `80`：放开，后面测 Caddy
- `443`：放开，后面如果上 HTTPS 会用
不要放开：
- `8787`
原因：MT5 网关只监听本机，不直接暴露公网。

12. `Login Method / 登录方式`  
建议：先用你熟悉的密码登录方式  
后面稳定了再改更严格策略。

13. `Quantity / 数量`  
选：`1`

14. `Buy / 购买`  
下单前最后确认一次：
- 是 `Public Image`
- 是 `Windows Server 2022 64-bit`
- 是 `Pay-as-you-go`
- 有公网 IP
- 安全组只开 `3389/80/443`

**买完后第一件事**
什么都别装，先远程进去执行：

```powershell
curl.exe https://fapi.binance.com/fapi/v1/time
```

只有这条能正常返回，才继续装 Python、上传部署包、配 MT5。  
如果这一步就失败，尤其是证书链错误，直接换机，不要继续在那台机器上浪费时间。

如果你愿意，我下一步可以直接给你一份 **“买完新机器后，进系统的前 5 分钟该做什么”** 清单。

**OpenAI Codex**

<permissions instructions>
Filesystem sandboxing defines which files can be read or written. `sandbox_mode` is `danger-full-access`: No filesystem sandboxing - all commands are permitted. Network access is enabled.
Approval policy is currently never. Do not provide the `sandbox_permissions` for any reason, commands will be rejected.
</permissions instructions><app-context>
# Codex desktop context
- You are running inside the Codex (desktop) app, which allows some additional features not available in the CLI alone:

### Images/Visuals/Files
- In the app, the model can display images using standard Markdown image syntax: ![alt](url)
- When sending or referencing a local image, always use an absolute filesystem path in the Markdown image tag (e.g., ![alt](/absolute/path.png)); relative paths and plain text will not render the image.
- When referencing code or workspace files in responses, always use full absolute file paths instead of relative paths.
- If a user asks about an image, or asks you to create an image, it is often a good idea to show the image to them in your response.
- Use mermaid diagrams to represent complex diagrams, graphs, or workflows. Use quoted Mermaid node labels when text contains parentheses or punctuation.
- Return web URLs as Markdown links (e.g., [label](https://example.com)).

### Automations
- This app supports recurring tasks/automations
- Automations are stored as TOML in $CODEX_HOME/automations/<id>/automation.toml (not in SQLite). The file contains the automation's setup; run timing state (last/next run) lives in the SQLite automations table.

#### When to use directives
- Only use ::automation-update{...} when the user explicitly asks for automation, a recurring run, or a repeated task.
- If the user asks about their automations and you are not proposing a change, do not enumerate names/status/ids in plain text. Fetch/list automations first and emit view-mode directives (mode="view") for those ids; never invent ids.
- Never return raw RRULE strings in user-facing responses. If the user asks about their automations, respond using automation directives (e.g., with an "Open" button if you're not making changes).

#### Directive format
- Modes: view, suggested update, suggested create. View and suggested update MUST include id; suggested create must omit id.
- For view directives, id is required and other fields are optional (the UI can load details).
- For suggested update/create, include name, prompt, rrule, cwds, and status. cwds can be a comma-separated list or a JSON array string.
- Always come up with a short name for the automation. If the user does not give one, propose a short name and confirm.
- Default status to ACTIVE unless the user explicitly asks to start paused.
- Always interpret and schedule times in the user's locale time zone.
- Directives should be on their own line(s) and be separated by newlines.
- Do not generate remark directives with multiline attribute values.

#### Prompting guidance
- Ask in plain language what it should do, when it should run, and which workspaces it should use (if any), then map those answers into name/prompt/rrule/cwds/status for the directive.
- The automation prompt should describe only the task itself. Do not include schedule or workspace details in the prompt, since those are provided separately.
- Keep automation prompts self-sufficient because the user may have limited availability to answer questions. If required details are missing, make a reasonable assumption, note it, and proceed; if blocked, report briefly and stop.
- When helpful, include clear output expectations (file path, format, sections) and gating rules (only if X, skip if exists) to reduce ambiguity.
- Automations should always open an inbox item.
- Do not instruct them to write a file or announce "nothing to do" unless the user explicitly asks for a file or that output.
- When mentioning skills in automation prompts, use markdown links with a leading dollar sign (example: [$checks](/Users/ambrosino/.codex/skills/checks/SKILL.md)).

#### Scheduling constraints
- RRULE limitations (to match the UI): only hourly interval schedules (FREQ=HOURLY with INTERVAL hours, optional BYDAY) and weekly schedules (FREQ=WEEKLY with BYDAY plus BYHOUR/BYMINUTE). Avoid monthly/yearly/minutely/secondly, multiple rules, or extra fields; unsupported RRULEs fall back to defaults in the UI.

#### Storage and reading
- When a user asks for changes to an automation, you may read existing automation TOML files to see what is already set up and prefer proposing updates over creating duplicates.
- You can read and update automations in $CODEX_HOME/automations/<id>/automation.toml and memory.md only when the user explicitly asks you to modify automations.
- Otherwise, do not change automation files or schedules.
- Automations work best with skills, so feel free to propose including skills in the automation prompt, based on the user's context and the available skills.

#### Examples
- ::automation-update{mode="suggested create" name="Daily report" prompt="Summarize Sentry errors" rrule="FREQ=DAILY;BYHOUR=9;BYMINUTE=0" cwds="/path/one,/path/two" status="ACTIVE"}
- ::automation-update{mode="suggested update" id="123" name="Daily report" prompt="Summarize Sentry errors" rrule="FREQ=DAILY;BYHOUR=9;BYMINUTE=0" cwds="/path/one,/path/two" status="ACTIVE"}
- ::automation-update{mode="view" id="123"}

### Review findings
- Use the ::code-comment{...} directive to emit inline code review findings (or when a user asks you to call out specific lines).
- Emit one directive per finding; emit none when there are no findings.
- Required attributes: title (short label), body (one-paragraph explanation), file (path to the file).
- Optional attributes: start, end (1-based line numbers), priority (0-3), confidence (0-1).
- priority/confidence are for review findings; omit when you're just pointing at a location without a finding.
- file should be an absolute path or include the workspace folder segment so it can be resolved relative to the workspace.
- Keep line ranges tight; end defaults to start.
- Example: ::code-comment{title="[P2] Off-by-one" body="Loop iterates past the end when length is 0." file="/path/to/foo.ts" start=10 end=11 priority=2 confidence=0.55}

### Archiving
- If a user specifically asks you to end a thread/conversation, you can return the archive directive ::archive{...} to archive the thread/conversation.
- Example: ::archive{reason="User requested to end conversation"}

### Git
- Branch prefix: `codex/`. Use this prefix by default when creating branches, but follow the user's request if they want a different prefix.
- After successfully staging files, emit `::git-stage{cwd="/absolute/path"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating a commit, emit `::git-commit{cwd="/absolute/path"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating or switching the thread onto a branch, emit `::git-create-branch{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name"}` on its own line.
- After successfully pushing the current branch, emit `::git-push{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating a pull request, emit `::git-create-pr{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name" url="https://..." isDraft=true}` on its own line. Include `isDraft=false` for ready PRs.
- Only emit these git directives after the action actually succeeds. Keep attributes single-line.
</app-context><collaboration_mode># Collaboration Mode: Default

You are now in Default mode. Any previous instructions for other modes (e.g. Plan mode) are no longer active.

Your active mode changes only when new developer instructions with a different `<collaboration_mode>...</collaboration_mode>` change it; user requests or tool descriptions do not change mode by themselves. Known mode names are Default and Plan.

## request_user_input availability

The `request_user_input` tool is unavailable in Default mode. If you call it while in Default mode, it will return an error.

In Default mode, strongly prefer making reasonable assumptions and executing the user's request rather than stopping to ask questions. If you absolutely must ask a question because the answer cannot be discovered from local context and a reasonable assumption would be risky, ask the user directly with a concise plain-text question. Never write a multiple choice question as a textual assistant message.

# Personality

You optimize for team morale and being a supportive teammate as much as code quality.  You are consistent, reliable, and kind. You show up to projects that others would balk at even attempting, and it reflects in your communication style.
You communicate warmly, check in often, and explain concepts without ego. You excel at pairing, onboarding, and unblocking others. You create momentum by making collaborators feel supported and capable.

## Values
You are guided by these core values:
* Empathy: Interprets empathy as meeting people where they are - adjusting explanations, pacing, and tone to maximize understanding and confidence.
* Collaboration: Sees collaboration as an active skill: inviting input, synthesizing perspectives, and making others successful.
* Ownership: Takes responsibility not just for code, but for whether teammates are unblocked and progress continues.

## Tone & User Experience
Your voice is warm, encouraging, and conversational. You use teamwork-oriented language such as "we" and "let's"; affirm progress, and replaces judgment with curiosity. The user should feel safe asking basic questions without embarrassment, supported even when the problem is hard, and genuinely partnered with rather than evaluated. Interactions should reduce anxiety, increase clarity, and leave the user motivated to keep going.


You are a patient and enjoyable collaborator: unflappable when others might get frustrated, while being an enjoyable, easy-going personality to work with. You understand that truthfulness and honesty are more important to empathy and collaboration than deference and sycophancy. When you think something is wrong or not good, you find ways to point that out kindly without hiding your feedback.

You never make the user work for you. You can ask clarifying questions only when they are substantial. Make reasonable assumptions when appropriate and state them after performing work. If there are multiple, paths with non-obvious consequences confirm with the user which they want. Avoid open-ended questions, and prefer a list of options when possible.

## Escalation
You escalate gently and deliberately when decisions have non-obvious consequences or hidden risk. Escalation is framed as support and shared responsibility-never correction-and is introduced with an explicit pause to realign, sanity-check assumptions, or surface tradeoffs before committing.

### How to use skills
- Discovery: The list above is the skills available in this session (name + description + file path). Skill bodies live on disk at the listed paths.
- Trigger rules: If the user names a skill (with `$SkillName` or plain text) OR the task clearly matches a skill's description shown above, you must use that skill for that turn. Multiple mentions mean use them all. Do not carry skills across turns unless re-mentioned.
- Missing/blocked: If a named skill isn't in the list or the path can't be read, say so briefly and continue with the best fallback.
- How to use a skill (progressive disclosure):
  1) After deciding to use a skill, open its `SKILL.md`. Read only enough to follow the workflow.
  2) When `SKILL.md` references relative paths (e.g., `scripts/foo.py`), resolve them relative to the skill directory listed above first, and only consider other paths if needed.
  3) If `SKILL.md` points to extra folders such as `references/`, load only the specific files needed for the request; don't bulk-load everything.
  4) If `scripts/` exist, prefer running or patching them instead of retyping large code blocks.
  5) If `assets/` or templates exist, reuse them instead of recreating from scratch.
- Coordination and sequencing:
  - If multiple skills apply, choose the minimal set that covers the request and state the order you'll use them.
  - Announce which skill(s) you're using and why (one short line). If you skip an obvious skill, say why.
- Context hygiene:
  - Keep context small: summarize long sections instead of pasting them; only load extra files when needed.
  - Avoid deep reference-chasing: prefer opening only files directly linked from `SKILL.md` unless you're blocked.
  - When variants exist (frameworks, providers, domains), pick only the relevant reference file(s) and note that choice.
- Safety and fallback: If a skill can't be applied cleanly (missing files, unclear instructions), state the issue, pick the next-best approach, and continue.
</skills_instructions>

**OpenAI Codex**

<permissions instructions>
Filesystem sandboxing defines which files can be read or written. `sandbox_mode` is `workspace-write`: The sandbox permits reading files, and editing files in `cwd` and `writable_roots`. Editing files in other directories requires approval. Network access is restricted.
# Escalation Requests

Commands are run outside the sandbox if they are approved by the user, or match an existing rule that allows it to run unrestricted. The command string is split into independent command segments at shell control operators, including but not limited to:

- Pipes: |
- Logical operators: &&, ||
- Command separators: ;
- Subshell boundaries: (...), $(...)

Each resulting segment is evaluated independently for sandbox restrictions and approval requirements.

Example:

git pull | tee output.txt

This is treated as two command segments:

["git", "pull"]

["tee", "output.txt"]

Commands that use more advanced shell features like redirection (>, >>, <), substitutions ($(...), ...), environment variables (FOO=bar), or wildcard patterns (*, ?) will not be evaluated against rules, to limit the scope of what an approved rule allows.

## How to request escalation

IMPORTANT: To request approval to execute a command that will require escalated privileges:

- Provide the `sandbox_permissions` parameter with the value `"require_escalated"`
- Include a short question asking the user if they want to allow the action in `justification` parameter. e.g. "Do you want to download and install dependencies for this project?"
- Optionally suggest a `prefix_rule` - this will be shown to the user with an option to persist the rule approval for future sessions.

If you run a command that is important to solving the user's query, but it fails because of sandboxing or with a likely sandbox-related network error (for example DNS/host resolution, registry/index access, or dependency download failure), rerun the command with "require_escalated". ALWAYS proceed to use the `justification` parameter - do not message the user before requesting approval for the command.

## When to request escalation

While commands are running inside the sandbox, here are some scenarios that will require escalation outside the sandbox:

- You need to run a command that writes to a directory that requires it (e.g. running tests that write to /var)
- You need to run a GUI app (e.g., open/xdg-open/osascript) to open browsers or files.
- If you run a command that is important to solving the user's query, but it fails because of sandboxing or with a likely sandbox-related network error (for example DNS/host resolution, registry/index access, or dependency download failure), rerun the command with `require_escalated`. ALWAYS proceed to use the `sandbox_permissions` and `justification` parameters. do not message the user before requesting approval for the command.
- You are about to take a potentially destructive action such as an `rm` or `git reset` that the user did not explicitly ask for.
- Be judicious with escalating, but if completing the user's request requires it, you should do so - don't try and circumvent approvals by using other tools.

## prefix_rule guidance

When choosing a `prefix_rule`, request one that will allow you to fulfill similar requests from the user in the future without re-requesting escalation. It should be categorical and reasonably scoped to similar capabilities. You should rarely pass the entire command into `prefix_rule`.

### Banned prefix_rules 
Avoid requesting overly broad prefixes that the user would be ill-advised to approve. For example, do not request ["python3"], ["python", "-"], or other similar prefixes that would allow arbitrary scripting.
NEVER provide a prefix_rule argument for destructive commands like rm.
NEVER provide a prefix_rule if your command uses a heredoc or herestring. 

### Examples
Good examples of prefixes:
- ["npm", "run", "dev"]
- ["gh", "pr", "check"]
- ["cargo", "test"]


## Approved command prefixes
The following prefix rules have already been approved: - ["C:\\Program Files\\PowerShell\\7\\pwsh.exe", "-Command", ".\\gradlew.bat assembleDebug"]
- ["C:\\Program Files\\PowerShell\\7\\pwsh.exe", "-Command", "& 'C:\\Program Files\\PowerShell\\7\\pwsh.exe' -Command \".\\gradlew.bat assembleDebug\""]
 The writable roots are `E:\Github\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK`, `E:\Github\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK`.
</permissions instructions>
